     411             : 
     412             : /*
     413             : The limiter is used specifically for the text areas and textfields
     414             : In that case it is the DIV tag that is anonymously created for the text
     415             : areas/fields.  Text nodes and BR nodes fall beneath it.  In the case of a 
     416             : BR node the limiter will be the parent and the offset will point before or
     417             : after the BR node.  In the case of the text node the parent content is 
     418             : the text node itself and the offset will be the exact character position.
     419             : The offset is not important to check for validity.  Simply look at the 
     420             : passed in content.  If it equals the limiter then the selection point is valid.
     421             : If its parent it the limiter then the point is also valid.  In the case of 
     422             : NO limiter all points are valid since you are in a topmost iframe. (browser
     423             : or composer)
     424             : */

    4587             : 
    4588             : // Selection::LookUpSelection
    4589             : //
    4590             : //    This function is called when a node wants to know where the selection is
    4591             : //    over itself.
    4592             : //
    4593             : //    Usually, this is called when we already know there is a selection over
    4594             : //    the node in question, and we only need to find the boundaries of it on
    4595             : //    that node. This is when slowCheck is false--a strict test is not needed.
    4596             : //    Other times, the caller has no idea, and wants us to test everything,
    4597             : //    so we are supposed to determine whether there is a selection over the
    4598             : //    node at all.
    4599             : //
    4600             : //    A previous version of this code used this flag to do less work when
    4601             : //    inclusion was already known (slowCheck=false). However, our tree
    4602             : //    structure allows us to quickly determine ranges overlapping the node,
    4603             : //    so we just ignore the slowCheck flag and do the full test every time.
    4604             : //
    4605             : //    PERFORMANCE: a common case is that we are doing a fast check with exactly
    4606             : //    one range in the selection. In this case, this function is slower than
    4607             : //    brute force because of the overhead of checking the tree. We can optimize
    4608             : //    this case to make it faster by doing the same thing the previous version
    4609             : //    of this function did in the case of 1 range. This would also mean that
    4610             : //    the aSlowCheck flag would have meaning again.
    4611             : 
    4612             : UniquePtr<SelectionDetails>
    4613           1 : Selection::LookUpSelection(nsIContent* aContent, int32_t aContentOffset,
    4614             :                            int32_t aContentLength,
    4615             :                            UniquePtr<SelectionDetails> aDetailsHead,
    4616             :                            SelectionType aSelectionType,
    4617             :                            bool aSlowCheck)
    4618             : {
    4619           1 :   if (!aContent) {
    4620             :     return aDetailsHead;
    4621             :   }
    4622             : 
    4623             :   // it is common to have no ranges, to optimize that

    4626             :   }

    5057             : 
    5058             : // Selection::RemoveRange
    5059             : //
    5060             : //    Removes the given range from the selection. The tricky part is updating
    5061             : //    the flags on the frames that indicate whether they have a selection or
    5062             : //    not. There could be several selection ranges on the frame, and clearing
    5063             : //    the bit would cause the selection to not be drawn, even when there is
    5064             : //    another range on the frame (bug 346185).
    5065             : //
    5066             : //    We therefore find any ranges that intersect the same nodes as the range
    5067             : //    being removed, and cause them to set the selected bits back on their
    5068             : //    selected frames after we've cleared the bit from ours.
    5069             : 
    5070             : nsresult
    5071           1 : Selection::RemoveRange(nsIDOMRange* aDOMRange)
    5072             : {
    5073           1 :   if (!aDOMRange) {
    5074             :     return NS_ERROR_INVALID_ARG;
    5075             :   }
    5076           1 :   nsRange* range = static_cast<nsRange*>(aDOMRange);
    5077             :   ErrorResult result;
    5078           1 :   RemoveRange(*range, result);
    5079           1 :   return result.StealNSResult();
    5080             : }

    5508             : Notes which might come in handy for extend:
    5509             : 
    5510             : We can tell the direction of the selection by asking for the anchors selection
    5511             : if the begin is less than the end then we know the selection is to the "right".
    5512             : else it is a backwards selection.
    5513             : a = anchor
    5514             : 1 = old cursor
    5515             : 2 = new cursor
    5516             : 
    5517             :   if (a <= 1 && 1 <=2)    a,1,2  or (a1,2)
    5518             :   if (a < 2 && 1 > 2)     a,2,1
    5519             :   if (1 < a && a <2)      1,a,2
    5520             :   if (a > 2 && 2 >1)      1,2,a
    5521             :   if (2 < a && a <1)      2,a,1
    5522             :   if (a > 1 && 1 >2)      2,1,a
    5523             : then execute
    5524             : a  1  2 select from 1 to 2
    5525             : a  2  1 deselect from 2 to 1
    5526             : 1  a  2 deselect from 1 to a select from a to 2
    5527             : 1  2  a deselect from 1 to 2
    5528             : 2  1  a = continue selection from 2 to 1
    5529             : */

    6846           1 : NS_IMPL_ISUPPORTS(nsAutoCopyListener, nsISelectionListener)
    6847             : 
    6848             : /*
    6849             :  * What we do now:
    6850             :  * On every selection change, we copy to the clipboard anew, creating a
    6851             :  * HTML buffer, a transferable, an nsISupportsString and
    6852             :  * a huge mess every time.  This is basically what nsPresShell::DoCopy does
    6853             :  * to move the selection into the clipboard for Edit->Copy.
    6854             :  * 
    6855             :  * What we should do, to make our end of the deal faster:
    6856             :  * Create a singleton transferable with our own magic converter.  When selection
    6857             :  * changes (use a quick cache to detect ``real'' changes), we put the new
    6858             :  * nsISelection in the transferable.  Our magic converter will take care of
    6859             :  * transferable->whatever-other-format when the time comes to actually
    6860             :  * hand over the clipboard contents.
    6861             :  *
    6862             :  * Other issues:
    6863             :  * - which X clipboard should we populate?
    6864             :  * - should we use a different one than Edit->Copy, so that inadvertant
    6865             :  *   selections (or simple clicks, which currently cause a selection
    6866             :  *   notification, regardless of if they're in the document which currently has
    6867             :  *   selection!) don't lose the contents of the ``application''?  Or should we
    6868             :  *   just put some intelligence in the ``is this a real selection?'' code to
    6869             :  *   protect our selection against clicks in other documents that don't create
    6870             :  *   selections?
    6871             :  * - maybe we should just never clear the X clipboard?  That would make this 
    6872             :  *   problem just go away, which is very tempting.
    6873             :  *
    6874             :  * On macOS,
    6875             :  * nsIClipboard::kSelectionCache is the flag for current selection cache.
    6876             :  * Set the current selection cache on the parent process in
    6877             :  * widget cocoa nsClipboard whenever selection changes.
    6878             :  */
    6879             :
